Leading in the Age of AI: A Conversation with NVIDIA CEO Jensen Huang | Global Conference 2026

Milken Institute(94.2K) ·46:21 ·39.0K views · 2026-05-05
Jensen Huang (CEO, NVIDIA)
The AI revolution has transitioned from simple generative tools to "Agentic AI" capable of reasoning and planning, a shift that requires 1,000x more computational power and presents a multi-trillion-dollar opportunity for U.S.
TL;DR The AI revolution has transitioned from simple generative tools to "Agentic AI" capable of reasoning and planning, a shift that requires 1,000x more computational power and presents a multi-trillion-dollar opportunity for U.S. re-industrialization and power grid...

TL;DR

The AI revolution has transitioned from simple generative tools to "Agentic AI" capable of reasoning and planning, a shift that requires 1,000x more computational power and presents a multi-trillion-dollar opportunity for U.S. re-industrialization and power grid modernization.

The Evolution of AI: From Generation to Agency

  • The Shift to Agentic AI: Jensen Huang notes that while ChatGPT introduced Generative AI, the industry has moved into "Agentic AI"—systems that can understand, reason, plan, and use tools to execute productive work (e.g., software coding).
      • Tokens as Thoughts: Huang explains that "thinking" requires generating thoughts/tokens; once AI could generate, it could reason.
      • Reasoning vs. Retrieval: Future computing will shift from "retrieval-based" (fetching pre-recorded data) to "intention-based," where computers generate contextually relevant responses and plans in real-time.
  • The 1,000x Compute Jump: Agentic systems require roughly 1,000 times more computation than simple generative models.
      • This massive demand has caused GPU prices to appreciate "faster than good wine."
      • Hardware systems are evolving into "AI Factories"—massive racks (three tons each, $4M–$5M) containing millions of parts and seven different types of chips.

Economic Impact and Re-industrialization

  • U.S. Re-industrialization: Huang views AI as a multi-trillion-dollar opportunity to rebuild the American industrial base through three types of plants: chip plants, computer plants, and AI factories.
      • Market Forces: He emphasizes using market demand rather than just subsidies to drive manufacturing back to the U.S.
  • Modernizing the Power Grid: The AI boom provides the necessary "market forces" and paying customers to finally fund the modernization of the antiquated U.S. power grid and invest in sustainable energy, including nuclear.
  • NVIDIA’s Investment Strategy: The company invests across a "five-layer cake" (Energy, Infrastructure, Land/Shell, Models, and Applications).
      • NVIDIA targets "strategic points" where a $1 investment can activate $100 of ecosystem growth.
      • Early investments in infrastructure companies (e.g., CoreWeave, Lambda) were designed to provide "anchor" confidence to other investors.

Safety, Geopolitics, and Cybersecurity

  • The "Pragmatist" View on Safety: Huang rejects "AI Doomer" narratives, comparing AI safety to aviation. Safety is achieved through redundant systems, guardrails, and real-world testing.
  • Global Accessibility: Huang argues that while the U.S. should maintain the "first and best" technology, AI should be exported globally to maximize American economic and national security.
      • The "Nuke Test": He distinguishes AI from weapons of mass destruction: "100% of you need AI. None of you should have a nuke."
  • Cybersecurity via Open Source: To defend against "super-force" AI threats, Huang advocates for an "abundance of cheap force."
      • White Blood Cells: Open-source models can act as "swarms of white blood cells" to detect and close vulnerabilities faster than a single high-end model can exploit them.
  • Regulation: Huang supports regulation at the application level—treating AI-driven medical devices or self-driving cars with the same rigor as their traditional counterparts (e.g., "licensing" a self-driving car).

The Future of Work and Human Ambition

  • Job Dislocation vs. Transformation: Huang argues that AI won't eliminate professions but will transform them.
      • The Radiologist Example: A decade ago, experts predicted AI would replace radiologists. Instead, AI integrated into the workflow, allowing radiologists to see more patients and focus on diagnosis rather than just "studying scans."
  • Purpose vs. Task: Huang defines work as a series of tasks tied to a purpose. AI automates tasks (typing, scanning, coding), but humans retain the "purpose" (solving disease, treating patients, building companies).
  • A New Level of Ambition: Huang concludes that AI will accelerate scientific discovery by turning months of research into a single day of work.
      • The 100x Rule: He advises leaders to increase their expectations and ambitions by 100x because the limitations of the past no longer apply.
"The fundamental thing that everybody's missing... is that they misunderstand that the purpose of a job and the task of the job are related, not the same. Studying the scan is just a task you do. Your purpose in life is to work with doctors to help treat patients." — Jensen Huang
"The best answer for [a super-force AI threat] is actually open source... so that we have swarms of white blood cells... You can’t count on the fact that your AI is better than their AI. But you can count on the fact that you got more AI than they got." — Jensen Huang
"Whatever level of ambition you have, it's just not high enough. The fundamental change that we have to make... is whatever expectations I have for the company, you've got to increase it by about 100x." — Jensen Huang

A Conversation with Citadel’s Ken Griffin | Global Conference 2026

Milken Institute(94.2K) ·31:22 ·24.2K views · 2026-05-05
Ken Griffin (Founder and CEO, Citadel)
Ken Griffin views the U.S.
TL;DR Ken Griffin views the U.S. economy as uniquely resilient due to energy independence and a technology-driven productivity boom, though he warns that persistent inflation and declining urban safety standards necessitate a strategic shift toward business-friendly hubs like...

TL;DR

Ken Griffin views the U.S. economy as uniquely resilient due to energy independence and a technology-driven productivity boom, though he warns that persistent inflation and declining urban safety standards necessitate a strategic shift toward business-friendly hubs like Miami.

Geopolitics and the Energy Shield

  • Energy Independence: Griffin credits "American ingenuity" and fracking for making the U.S. a net energy consumer independent of global shocks.
      • While the U.S. is shielded, developing nations like Pakistan and Bangladesh face "literal curtailment" of energy, which risks a global recession if stalemates in the Middle East persist.
  • Iranian Containment: Griffin applauds the administration’s efforts to set back Iranian nuclear ambitions, viewing a nuclear Iran as a primary threat to national security.
  • The "Venezuela Success": He characterizes the recent political shift in Venezuela as a major foreign policy achievement, bringing a massive oil producer back into the U.S. strategic orbit.

Economic Outlook: Inflation and the Fed

  • Persistent Inflation: Griffin highlights a six-year decline in the dollar's purchasing power, citing "triggering" price increases such as a McDonald’s Coke rising from $0.99 to $2.50 and eggs reaching $8.00.
  • Monetary Policy: He believes the Federal Reserve will remain "on hold" for the remainder of the year.
      • Reasoning: Core inflation remains above target, the labor market is strengthening, and energy price shocks have tilted risks to the upside.
  • Productivity as a Solution: Griffin argues that the only path to long-term prosperity is increasing productivity through deregulation, R&D, and improved education.

The Technology Boom and AI Transformation

  • The C-Suite "Digitization" Trend: Griffin suggests the current "AI boom" is actually a broader technology boom.
      • AI has served as a catalyst for CEOs to re-evaluate all business processes, even if the eventual solutions rely on standard technology rather than generative AI.
  • Labor Market Shocks: While AI will create new categories of jobs (analogous to the rise of web designers), Griffin warns that "mid-career shocks" for roles like translators are being ignored by policy-makers.
  • The "Manhattan Project" of a Generation: Griffin’s view is that the AI revolution is a critical competitive race against China, requiring the concentrated talent of the world’s most gifted individuals.

Urban Governance and the "Miami Move"

  • The Decline of Chicago: Griffin describes his exit from Illinois as a response to "pointlessly hopeless" leadership and rampant violent crime.
      • Safety Concerns: He cited 25 bullet holes in his building’s ground floor and the attempted carjacking of his security detail as factors that made recruiting impossible.
  • New York vs. Miami: Despite plans for a $6 billion office tower at 350 Park Avenue, Griffin expressed deep concern over New York’s current political trajectory, specifically criticizing moves to dismantle gifted education programs.
      • Strategic Pivot: Citadel is "doubling down" on Miami because the Florida government embraces "earned success" rather than "redistributive handouts."

Education and Talent Acquisition

  • National Emergency: Griffin views the state of American education as a national security issue. He praises Mississippi’s "back to basics" approach (phonics and ending social promotion) which moved the state into the top 10 for education nationally.
  • Hiring Criteria: When recruiting for Citadel, Griffin prioritizes:
      • Grit and Perseverance: He specifically looks for athletes who have experienced loss and managed high-pressure time constraints.
      • Lifetime Learners: Because the rate of technological change is accelerating (2x the speed of previous generations), the ability to adapt is the most valuable skill for new graduates.

***

Notable Quotes

"Higher productivity is the path to prosperity. And we need to increase productivity in our country. We do that through deregulation, we do that through investments in research and development, we do that through educating our children." — Ken Griffin
"What did it feel like in Chicago with [Governor] JB Pritzker? It felt like being a salmon swimming upstream to die... it just felt very pointlessly hopeless." — Ken Griffin
"We as a country need to take a step back: what works to create prosperity and productivity, and we need to embrace those concepts and push them across our country. We need a little less polarizing rhetoric from Washington and a lot more focus on just thoughtful problem solving." — Ken Griffin

LIVE: VP Vance Speaks in Iowa

One America News Network(1.4M) ·33:45 ·863 views · 2026-05-05
JD Vance (Vice President)
Vice President JD Vance’s address in Iowa frames the upcoming elections as a choice between "common sense" populist representation and a Democrat party he claims prioritizes illegal immigrants and foreign interests over American workers.
TL;DR Vice President JD Vance’s address in Iowa frames the upcoming elections as a choice between "common sense" populist representation and a Democrat party he claims prioritizes illegal immigrants and foreign interests over American workers. The briefing highlights aggressive...

TL;DR

Vice President JD Vance’s address in Iowa frames the upcoming elections as a choice between "common sense" populist representation and a Democrat party he claims prioritizes illegal immigrants and foreign interests over American workers. The briefing highlights aggressive anti-fraud initiatives, protectionist trade policies for Iowa farmers, and the re-election of Congressman Zach Nunn as the primary vehicle for this agenda.

Economic Protectionism and Manufacturing

  • Combating Foreign Trade Abuses: Vance emphasized a shift away from decades of "dumping" by the People's Republic of China, which he argues historically undercut Iowa wages and closed local factories.
      • Tariff Strategy: The administration utilizes "big fat tariffs" to protect domestic jobs, ensuring foreign competitors pay for market access while local manufacturers receive tax breaks.
  • Tax Policy Results: The Working Families Tax Cut is credited with providing businesses the capital to expand, increase salaries, and issue higher bonuses.
      • Direct Impact: Vance noted that since the administration took office, the average American family is reportedly $1,300 richer due to combined tax and housing policies.

Government Accountability and the National Fraud Task Force

  • Aggressive Oversight: As leader of the federal fraud task force, Vance described uncovering systemic corruption as "fishing in a barrel with dynamite."
  • SNAP Benefit Reform: Secretary of Agriculture Brooke Rollins identified significant misappropriation of food stamps, including:
      • Deceased Recipients: 186,000 dead individuals currently receiving benefits.
      • Benefit Doubling: 355,000 individuals receiving double SNAP benefits.
      • Wealth Disparity: Instances of individuals owning luxury vehicles (Lamborghinis) while remaining on the SNAP rolls.
  • Audit Enforcement: The administration has issued 22 subpoenas through the Department of Justice to investigate fraud, specifically citing a case in Minnesota where funds meant for autistic children were allegedly diverted to "Somalian fraudsters."

Housing and Border Security

  • Housing Affordability: Vance linked the high cost of rent and homeownership to foreign investment and illegal immigration.
      • Policy Principle: The administration advocates for the principle that "American homes belong to American families," not foreign investors or Chinese entities buying domestic farmland.
  • Supply and Demand: He argued that the housing crisis can be mitigated by ending the practice of providing housing to an estimated "30 million illegal aliens" and instead securing the border to stabilize costs for young citizens.

Iowa Agriculture and Local Representation

  • Market Expansion: Vance claimed that trade authorities have doubled the export market for Iowa farmers in the last 18 months by forcing foreign countries to accept Iowa products in exchange for US market access.
  • Energy Independence: He expressed strong support for E15 fuel, noting that Congressman Zach Nunn is currently advancing legislation to broaden its market reach.
  • Candidate Contrast: Vance sharply criticized Nunn’s opponent, Sarah Trone Garriott, for focusing on "far-left" social issues—such as gender transition policies in schools—rather than economic priorities like E15 expansion, fertilizer costs, or take-home pay.

National Service and Moral Obligations

  • Veterans and Gold Star Families: Reflecting on a meeting with families of service members killed in Iran and Syria, Vance argued that political leadership must be "worthy of the sacrifice" made by the military.
  • The "Earn This" Standard: Citing the film *Saving Private Ryan*, Vance stated that the primary duty of elected officials is to honor the fallen by waking up every day to fight for the American people’s interests rather than personal enrichment or insider trading.
"Finding fraud in the federal government is kind of like fishing in a barrel with dynamite. Every week I get a report... and I am shocked every single day by the things that we find." — VP JD Vance

Investing in The AI Era, Lessons from China, & Career Advice in 2026 | Bill Gurley

The Room Where It Happened(23.2K) ·47:06 ·132 views · 2026-05-05
Bill Gurley (Investor) Jake Humphrey (Host, The Room Where It Happened)
Bill Gurley argues that AI is an "infinite game" where the greatest risk is professional inaction; success in this era requires "high agency" curiosity to use AI as a productivity "jet pack" rather than a tool to bypass learning.
TL;DR Bill Gurley argues that AI is an "infinite game" where the greatest risk is professional inaction; success in this era requires "high agency" curiosity to use AI as a productivity "jet pack" rather than a tool to bypass learning. The Cost of Inaction: Citing Daniel...

TL;DR

Bill Gurley argues that AI is an "infinite game" where the greatest risk is professional inaction; success in this era requires "high agency" curiosity to use AI as a productivity "jet pack" rather than a tool to bypass learning.

Career Regret and the Power of Fascination

  • The Cost of Inaction: Citing Daniel Pink, Gurley emphasizes that as people age, they rarely regret mistakes; they regret "boldness regrets" or things they never tried.
  • The Fascination Superpower: Modern education and "industrial education complexes" have traded exploration for perceived safety.
      • The Resume Arms Race: Kids are overscheduled (Mandarin, cello, sports) to get into the "right lane," which leads to early burnout.
      • Decision Timing: In the US, students are often forced to choose a major at 17 rather than 20, shrinking the window for worldly discovery.
  • High Agency vs. Anxiety: Having "AI anxiety" is a low-agency response. Gurley argues that if you aren't curious about how AI can improve your work, you may be in the wrong career.

The AI Investment Landscape: Bubbles vs. Reality

  • Valuation Anomalies: OpenAI and Anthropic are reaching valuations near $1 trillion as private companies, raising $100B+—figures 20–25x larger than any previous venture cycles.
  • The "Realness" of the Bubble: Gurley dismisses the idea that massive data center spending proves AI is a fad.
      • Historical Context: Successful technology waves and bubbles always happen simultaneously.
      • Directional Correctness: Speculators and "charlatans" enter when people get rich quick, but the heavy investment exists precisely because the technology is transformative.
  • The Innovator's Dilemma: Google and Microsoft failed to "get the jump" because they were protecting "cash flow printing machines." Taking the risks required to lead AI would have meant putting their primary revenue at risk.

Geopolitics: The US vs. China

  • Two Divergent Models:
      • United States: Focused on proprietary, closed-loop models (OpenAI, Anthropic).
      • China: Driven by government-encouraged open-source development.
  • The Long-Term Victor: Gurley suggests that China’s open-source approach may eventually "catch and pass" US proprietary models because open systems learn from one another more efficiently over time.
  • The "Infinite Game" Fallacy: Gurley rejects the "China Hawk" narrative of winning an AI race.
      • No Finish Line: Like the "nuclear race," there is no official victor or whistle-blower.
      • Foolhardy Restrictions: Attempting to prevent a nation like China from developing AI is seen as impossible and counter-productive.

Regulation and Regulatory Capture

  • Skepticism of Governance: Gurley is a "no-regulation guy" regarding AI, citing the risk of Regulatory Capture.
      • Incumbent Influence: He warns that leaders like OpenAI and Anthropic are effectively writing the legislation to "improve their lot in life" and block smaller competitors.
      • The "Doomer" Narrative: He notes that Anthropic is a primary source of AI "fear-mongering," which fuels public anxiety and encourages restrictive state-level regulation.
  • Legislative Ignorance: Politicians are attempting to regulate technology they do not understand, often influenced by the very companies they are meant to oversee.

Practical Strategies for 2026

  • Learning vs. Skipping: Gurley highlights Mark Cuban’s distinction: use LLMs to learn faster, not to skip the learning process entirely.
  • The "Sitting Duck" Risk: If you are one of 30 people doing the same job, the only way to protect yourself from disruption is to be the most "AI-enabled" version of yourself.
  • Concrete Use Cases:
      • Multimodal Troubleshooting: Take photos of broken devices or complex systems for instant AI diagnostics.
      • Strategic Preparation: High-level attorneys are using AI to predict specific questions from Supreme Court Justices with high accuracy.
      • Recursive Learning: Use AI to identify "orthogonal moves" in projects (e.g., asking for 10 successful non-fiction conclusions to rewrite a book chapter).
"Human beings are really good at forgiving themselves for making mistakes after the fact... but the thing they never tried is always out there weighing on their brain." — Bill Gurley
"If you're someone who's somewhat ambivalent about your job and you're not spending time trying to figure out how AI may make you more powerful in that role, you're a sitting duck." — Bill Gurley
"To say I'm going to win the AI race is like saying 'we're going to win the nuclear race.' When is the official going to blow the whistle and declare the victor? It doesn't happen." — Bill Gurley

I'm not sure there's ever a finish line to this. Well, Bill, thank you very much for joining us. In your new book you talk about this concept of avoiding career regret. Why do you think so many people struggle with career regret? You know, and Daniel Pink wrote a book about regret and he said in there that there's studies across the globe, so not just in the US, across like different cultures, different countries. And as people get older, the number one thing that kind of weighs on them is what he calls boldness regrets or regrets of inaction. And so it turns out humans are really good at forgiving themselves for making mistakes after the fact. They like rationalize it—oh I learned something, whatever. But the thing they never tried kind of is always out there weighing on their brain. And so it's a bit of a like behavioral science problem where, when people are young, it's easy to put off the thing that seems a little too bold. And then as you get older and you have more like restrictions on your time and your money, then it's, then it's harder to even, you know, consider that you could do that. And so it just, it never gets tried. Well, I I think it's interesting the question as as you talked about it because there's this amazing book by Carlota Perez where she makes the point that technology waves, successful technology waves and bubbles always happen at the same time. Property Play: Propy CEO on the blockchain revolution coming for real estate

CNBC Television(3.4M) ·30:40 ·628 views · 2026-05-05
Natalia Karayaneva (Founder and CEO, Propy) Diana Olick (Correspondent, CNBC)
Propy is leveraging blockchain and AI to transform real estate transactions into secure, "on-chain" settlements, reducing closing times from weeks to hours.
TL;DR Propy is leveraging blockchain and AI to transform real estate transactions into secure, "on-chain" settlements, reducing closing times from weeks to hours. Through a $100 million rollup strategy, the company is acquiring and modernizing traditional title companies to...

TL;DR

Propy is leveraging blockchain and AI to transform real estate transactions into secure, "on-chain" settlements, reducing closing times from weeks to hours. Through a $100 million rollup strategy, the company is acquiring and modernizing traditional title companies to create a high-efficiency, liquid marketplace for global property ownership.

The Blockchain and AI Integration

  • Blockchain Foundation: Uses public networks (Ethereum, Gnosis, Bitcoin) to record deeds and transactions via smart contracts.
      • Security: Data is immutable and encrypted; while the fact of a transaction is public, sensitive buyer/seller data remains private to prevent fraud.
      • Efficiency: Transactions that typically take 30 days can be settled within hours by automating title, escrow, and settlement pieces.
  • AI Agent "Avery": A production-grade AI agent designed to manage the transaction workflow 24/7.
      • Technical Reliability: Built with RAG (Retrieval-Augmented Generation) and MCP (Model Context Protocol) tooling to eliminate "hallucinations" and ensure deterministic workflows.
      • Operational Capabilities: Avery manages emails, extracts contract data, and conducts voice calls with lenders and HOAs to order mortgage payouts and approvals without human intervention.
      • Omnichannel Presence: Operates via voice and text; currently acts as an "escrow officer that never sleeps."

Strategic Growth and "Rollup" Strategy

  • $100 Million Credit Line: Propy is utilizing a $100 million raise to execute an AI-led rollup strategy, acquiring established, profitable title and escrow companies.
  • Modernization of Traditional Firms: By acquiring local players, Propy integrates their legacy operations into a blockchain-based platform, turning existing staff into "superhumans" who can handle significantly higher transaction volumes.
  • Market Expansion:
      • Current Footprint: Active in Florida (largest market), Colorado, Arizona, California, and Texas, with upcoming expansion into Mississippi.
      • Scaling Throughput: The goal is to increase per-person capacity from 20-40 transactions to 1,000 transactions through AI automation.
  • Revenue Projections: The company grew 6x in Q1 2024 compared to the previous year and anticipates a 10x increase in revenue by year-end.

The Rise of On-Chain Payments

  • Stablecoin Adoption: There is a significant increase in international buyers using stablecoins (USDC, USDT) for deposits to avoid the slow speed and high costs of international bank wires.
  • Legislative Legitimacy: The passage of the Gnosis Act in 2023 provided regulatory clarity for stablecoins, encouraging REITs and developers to adopt crypto-integrated settlements.
  • Institutional Interest: Propy recently acquired a company serving a REIT with $13 billion under management, using AI to automate processes for large-scale institutional portfolios.

Long-Term Vision: Liquidity and Sovereignty

  • Bloomberg-Like Terminal: Natalia Karayaneva envisions a future where all real estate classes—residential, commercial, and industrial—are liquid 24/7 on a unified digital terminal.
  • Property Rights as Democracy:
      • Decentralized Records: Drawing from her background in the Soviet Union, Karayaneva argues that decentralized blockchain records protect private property from government seizure or database hacking.
      • Economic Empowerment: In developing nations, on-chain recording allows landowners to prove ownership securely, enabling them to borrow against assets and fund small businesses.
"Internet moved information, blockchain will move value. It already is moving money, it’s moving treasuries... however, the real estate industry is still behind." — Natalia Karayaneva
"AI overall is not just a tool that will assist labor, it’s an operating layer that will absorb labor... We aim to become the Uber of real estate, the ultimate winner." — Natalia Karayaneva
"In order [for] any corporation, government in the future, any dictatorship to not get the homes from people, people have to own this record, and they have to own it in a decentralized way." — Natalia Karayaneva
Propy is a company that's working to modernize how real estate transactions are completed, and that's by using the blockchain and AI. It was co-founded by a serial entrepreneur and award-winning developer, CEO Natalia Karayaneva. Welcome to the Property Play. Thank you so much for having me. Of course. Whenever we use the word blockchain, some people get very excited about it in real estate, while other people's eyes roll back in their heads. I'm somewhere in the middle, I gotta say. Explain in the simplest terms, what does Propy do? Absolutely. Many people are actually trying to divide crypto from blockchain, but these are very interconnected technologies. Blockchain is this technology that allows us to record deeds and transactions, and it's impossible to change this data. It's impossible to hack blockchain. When we use AI and AI agents, we automate the transaction—the title and escrow, the settlement piece. But the blockchain, the smart contracts on blockchain, allow us to transfer ownership in the most secure manner. So you can do it in seconds instead of many days or even weeks that some of these transaction closings can take, right? That's correct. So you can do it a lot more cheap. Yes, we can save on time and cost. In fact, we did a couple of transactions within hours instead of a 30-day closing process. They were still just a couple of those, I think four or five that we've done. They're historic ones. I often compare it to Netflix. When Netflix decided that at some point the internet will be able to show and stream movies online, entirely online, nobody believed in it. They started selling movies online. So what Propy is doing today is we're doing title and escrow almost in a traditional way. Our consumers and clients and REITs don't even know that we have blockchain settlement. But one day, we know real estate will move on chain. Just like we stream movies, we'll stream ownership and value entirely on chain. Now, the blockchain, it's kind of like what I liken to a giant filing cabinet, right? It's just blocks in this cabinet, and it's mostly public, or are there private parts of the blockchain? There are public blockchains and private blockchains. We're strong believers in public blockchains—Ethereum, Gnosis, and other networks, and Bitcoin, of course. That's where you can publicly verify if one transaction has happened. However, when we talk about real estate transactions settled via smart contracts, the most sensitive data is invisible. We only see that, okay, this ownership has happened. So you can see who owns a property or who just purchased a property? Yes, but we don't see any sensitive private data about the buyer or the seller. Bank accounts, that kind of thing? Exactly. Everything is encrypted. So it's the kind of thing where if you were to call the county records to find out how much a home sold for, that would be public record, but you wouldn't have things like bank account numbers or names necessarily. You know, very specific private documentation would not be visible to the public on the blockchain. Yes, absolutely. I could give a very illustrative example. When we receive a purchase agreement signed about a home purchase, whether it's from REITs or from a real estate developer or from a realtor, our AI extracts the data—the critical terms, the purchase agreement, the address, all the contingencies, all the conditions—and then a smart contract on the blockchain starts. So anytime we ask about a buyer to transfer an earnest money deposit, we do it through our fintech solutions, but then the blockchain immediately gets this data on the public blockchain. Okay, there is one condition throughout this purchase timeline that has happened. It's recorded, but it's not publicly available to understand how much was transferred by whom and where. It allows us to be a fraud-less system. If something is happening in a transaction and we need to prove that none of the software engineers or hackers got into our system, we can always go to the blockchain and verify, yes, this transaction has happened. Then we decrypt what exactly has happened, but obviously in a private environment. So you believe it's completely safe. But it's interesting when I talk to real estate CEOs—some of them the older ones, more established, high-level CEOs, but even some younger ones—and I talk to them about blockchain and putting real estate transactions and tokenizing real estate on the blockchain, a lot of them say, "No, I don't trust it. I don't see the regulation for it. I don't want any part of it." Some people think it's just a fad—I don't want to say a fad—but they think it's something that is gonna be played out and is not for the long term. How do you counter their beliefs and how do you make really established real estate developers, CEOs, and investors trust what you're doing? That's a great question, and we had to deal with it for eight years. Since Propy launched in 2017, we had this conviction that blockchain is the next phenomenon after the internet. Internet moved information; blockchain will move value. It's already moving money and moving treasuries, like RWAs with the BlackRock bid. However, the real estate industry is still behind. Always has been. Always has been, yeah. That's why it's a trillion-dollar market just in the liquidity in real estate that hasn't been touched and changed for decades. But what shifted was last year. In 2023, when the Gnosis Act passed, suddenly the stablecoins—the most stable aspect of the crypto experience and crypto industry—finally gave this legitimacy to the market. Real estate developers and REITs started to reach out to Propy because we've established this brand for so many years with our strong conviction that there is a way to legally accept cryptocurrencies in real estate and to legally record deeds on the blockchain and in the county, of course. That suddenly unlocked, especially here in Miami, a huge interest by real estate developers. They see a specific need, which is international buyers, which is a big portion of real estate investors here in Florida. They need to transfer their funds for deposits, and deposits have to be available within a certain period of time. Wires internationally work very slow, and thus they see this sudden increase—and we see it at Propy—this sudden increase in transactions in stablecoin, like USDC and USDT, by people. Whose what? USDT. Like there are a number of stablecoins, it's not just one. Okay. So USDC transactions, payments for deposits in real estate transactions. Not just Bitcoin, but... Not just Bitcoin. Because everybody's kind of nervous about Bitcoin because it's so volatile. It goes up, it goes down, so they feel it's kind of like a game. But you're talking about much more stable currencies. Exactly. It's a stable currency; it's a cryptocurrency tied to the US dollar. So there is no fluctuation. We accept Bitcoin too; we transfer it and exchange it to dollars right away, and the developer gets the funds in their bank account right away, or we keep them in our escrow account. What we're seeing as a fascinating fact is that a lot of foreign real estate investors prefer us to educate them on cryptocurrency and stablecoin so they can transfer the funds right away the same day versus going to a bank and risking their transaction by doing wires. And so all of this new transparency and the new interest that you're seeing, that helped you to get a $100 million credit line last year. What are you gonna do with all that cash? Yeah, we're very excited. Last year, we raised $100 million for an AI-led rollup strategy. We are acquiring existing title and escrow companies so we have a faster distribution in key markets in the United States. So you're consolidating, buying up these old-fashioned title escrow companies and turning them into the modern tokenized way of doing real estate closings. Exactly. When we buy a profitable, very well-established local player in each market—we've bought already three and are about to close on the fourth one—they're fascinated by blockchain and cryptocurrency. They come to us because we know how to do those things compliantly. They also have a very big fear of AI. When we acquire them, we have this in-person training both on AI and blockchain and cryptocurrency. We have established courses and trainings for those escrow officers on how to do transactions. But once they understand and let the wheel go, the transaction happens on its own. AI opens a transaction 24/7, on the weekend, and in the evening. Okay, but I want to understand the AI part of it because every company I talk to now is implementing AI. Some, I see you rolling your eyes, but some of them, it's really just using data programs or software programs. But the real AI, you have an AI agent. Yeah, I will explain a little bit with the technical terms for your audience, and then we'll dumb it down to exactly how you can imagine it. I love it. Dumb it down as far as you can. Well, first of all, we've built a production-grade AI, not a co-pilot. It means that our AI agent orchestration is built on a tech stack with RAG, with persistent memory, and with MCP tooling. Okay, you're gonna need to translate what you just said. It means our AI agents don't experience hallucinations. Okay. It means they don't make mistakes. All the workflows are deterministic. We are controlling this previously human orchestration by a controlled autonomous workflow. So what it means practically is we've launched this AI agent Avery. She has a name. She's a she, of course. She's a she. She has an Instagram account, and she educates our community on what Propy is and what she is. She's an escrow officer that never sleeps. She checks emails every single day, 24/7, opens transactions 24/7, extracts all those data points and then feeds that data to our smart contract platform. She also makes calls. It's an omnichannel communication where she can communicate with our buyers, sellers, with REITs, institutional clients, and with vendors. For example, she is ordering mortgage payouts from lenders and she's getting approvals from HOAs. And actual human people are willing to talk to her? They don't recognize that she's not a human. Why? For AI innovation, almost any new shiny AI company can be disrupted by the frontier models. Vice President JD Vance Delivers Remarks in Des Moines, Iowa

The White House(3.1M) ·52:27 ·27.0K views · 2026-05-05
JD Vance (Vice President)
Vice President JD Vance and Congressman Zach Nunn met with manufacturing leaders in Des Moines to promote "America First" economic policies, highlighting the fight against Chinese intellectual property theft, the expansion of agricultural export mark...
TL;DR Vice President JD Vance and Congressman Zach Nunn met with manufacturing leaders in Des Moines to promote "America First" economic policies, highlighting the fight against Chinese intellectual property theft, the expansion of agricultural export markets, and a new federal...

TL;DR

Vice President JD Vance and Congressman Zach Nunn met with manufacturing leaders in Des Moines to promote "America First" economic policies, highlighting the fight against Chinese intellectual property theft, the expansion of agricultural export markets, and a new federal crackdown on government fraud.

Manufacturing and Trade Accountability

  • Combatting Industrial Espionage: Congressman Nunn highlighted the host venue, X-Guard, as a victim of intellectual property theft.
      • He alleged that Beijing "poached" American designs for tractor-trailer safety equipment and "dumped" the copied products back into the U.S. market to undercut domestic manufacturing.
  • Tariff Policy: Vice President Vance emphasized that current trade policy focuses on protecting American wages through "big fat tariffs" on foreign countries that utilize cheap or slave labor.
      • The administration’s stance is that domestic builders deserve tax cuts, while those dumping goods into the U.S. market should pay a premium to enter.
  • Domestic Success: X-Guard owners reported that tax cuts for working families directly allowed for higher worker bonuses and business expansion.

Agricultural Priorities and Rural Infrastructure

  • The Farm Bill: Congressman Nunn discussed the recent bipartisan movement of a Farm Bill that includes 21 specific Iowa priorities.
      • Biofuels: Legislation is moving forward to enable year-round, nationwide sales of E15 fuel.
      • Connectivity: A focus on rural broadband to support telehealth and autonomous farming technology.
      • Livestock Protections: Efforts to end animal torture and "puppy mills" by mirroring state-level legislation at the federal level.
  • Market Expansion: Vance reported that trade policies have doubled the export market for Iowa farmers in the last 18 months.
      • The administration used trade authorities to force foreign countries to stop dumping agricultural products and instead open their borders to U.S.-grown goods.

Federal Oversight and Government Reform

  • The Fraud Task Force: Vice President Vance, leading a federal fraud task force, reported significant findings in the SNAP (food stamps) program.
      • Specific Findings: Discoveries include 186,000 deceased individuals and 355,000 people receiving double benefits.
      • Enforcement: Vance noted the issuance of 22 investigative subpoenas in Minneapolis and stated that those defrauding the government will face prison time.
  • Legislative Ethics: Congressman Nunn advocated for the "Stock Act" to end insider trading among members of Congress.
      • He cited $200 million in stock trades by Congressional members in the last year as evidence of the need for reform, alongside proposals for term limits.

Economic Policy and National Security

  • Housing Affordability: Vance linked the rising cost of housing to foreign investment and illegal immigration.
      • He argued that by sealing the border and preventing foreign entities (specifically Chinese investors) from buying up farmland and residential homes, supply will return to American families.
  • Veterans and Gold Star Families: Both speakers addressed the disproportionate sacrifice of Iowa service members.
      • Vance emphasized a moral obligation to "earn" the sacrifice of fallen soldiers by ensuring the federal government remains worthy of their service and focused on its own citizens first.

Notable Quotes

"Our tax policy ought to be pretty simple... If you're building right here in Iowa... you deserve a tax cut. But if you're a foreign country dumping that garbage into our country... you're going to pay a big fat tariff." — Vice President JD Vance
"Not only did they want to put Sam and Ryan out of business, they were trying to put an American industry to bed so they could own that space going forward. I’m so proud... of holding bad actors accountable." — Congressman Zach Nunn
"We have to make this country's politics and government worthy of the people who put on the uniform and will never see their loved ones again." — Vice President JD Vance

Palantir Technologies | Q1 2026 Earnings Webcast

TL;DR Palantir delivered record-breaking Q1 2026 results featuring 85% year-over-year revenue growth and 104% growth in its US business, driven by the massive scale of its Artificial Intelligence Platform (AIP) and a strategic focus on "no-slop" operational AI. Revenue...

TL;DR

Palantir delivered record-breaking Q1 2026 results featuring 85% year-over-year revenue growth and 104% growth in its US business, driven by the massive scale of its Artificial Intelligence Platform (AIP) and a strategic focus on "no-slop" operational AI.

Financial Performance & Guidance

  • Revenue Growth: Total revenue grew 85% YoY to $1.633 billion, marking the 11th consecutive quarter of accelerating growth.
  • Rule of 40 Dominance: The company achieved a Rule of 40 score of 145 (up from 127 last quarter), driven by high margins and rapid expansion.
  • US Market Acceleration: The US business now accounts for 79% of total revenue.
      • US Commercial: Grew 133% YoY to $595 million.
      • US Government: Grew 84% YoY to $687 million.
  • Guidance Raise: Management raised the full-year 2026 revenue guidance midpoint to $7.656 billion (71% YoY growth), representing the largest guidance raise in the company’s history.
  • Profitability: Palantir maintained GAAP profitability for the 14th consecutive quarter, with a GAAP net income of $871 million (53% margin).

AIP Strategy: The "No-Slop" Zone

  • Operational AI vs. "AI Slop": CEO Alex Karp and CTO Shyam Sankar distinguished Palantir’s AIP from "AI slop"—unreliable, model-only solutions. They argued that for AI to provide value in "load-bearing" institutions (hospitals, war zones, factories), it requires an Ontology to ensure precision and auditability.
  • Jevons’ Paradox: Sankar noted that as the cost of tokens drops (1,000x cheaper over three years), demand for tokens is skyrocketing. AIP is positioned as the "train" for this "coal," using cheaper tokens to fuel complex, multi-step agentic workflows.
  • Agent Operating System: Palantir is shipping a platform-native Agent Engine SDK. This provides a unified layer for governing, auditing, and attributing costs to AI agents across an enterprise.
  • Death of Legacy Software: Management noted that customers are increasingly replacing static legacy systems (like CRMs) with AI-first solutions built on AIP in months rather than years.

US Commercial & Industrial Impact

  • Sector Deepening:
      • Insurance: AIG is using AIP for a multi-agentic underwriting and claims solution to detect fraud and evaluate risk.
      • Aerospace: GE Aerospace expanded its partnership to deploy agentic AI across military supply chains following a 26% increase in engine production.
      • Mortgage: Partners like Motor and Freedom Mortgage are using AIP to automate the end-to-end mortgage process to lower borrowing costs.
  • Efficiency Gains: Thomas Cavanagh Construction reported that 97% of its employees use Palantir's Foundry daily, rendering other software redundant.

Defense and Government Transformation

  • Maven Smart System: Usage of the Maven platform has quadrupled over the last 12 months, becoming the "default builder platform" for the Department of War.
  • Ship OS: In partnership with the Navy, Palantir has reduced manufacturing Bill of Materials (BOM) approval times from 200 hours to 15 seconds.
  • Agricultural Security: The USDA awarded Palantir a $300 million contract to protect agricultural programs from foreign influence and fraud.
  • The "Spud-Nik" Moment: Sankar described a massive shift in the AI arms race where models (Mythos and Spud) are identifying thousands of zero-day vulnerabilities. Palantir's Apollo is being positioned to provide autonomous remediation for these threats.

Operational Efficiency

  • Sales Force Leanliness: Alex Karp highlighted that Palantir is achieving triple-digit US growth with only 70 salespeople, whereas a typical company of its size would require 7,000.
  • Talent Density: The company continues to surge resources from commercial sectors into defense manufacturing (Warp Speed) to support the US maritime industrial base and ammunition production.

***

"Tokens are the new coal, AIP is the train. As inference gets cheaper, the number of tasks that you can economically assign to AI grows exponentially... But more tokens means more slop. And the more commodity cognition you consume, the more you need a system that can prevent the economic harm."

— Shyam Sankar, Chief Technology Officer

"Our free cash flow this quarter is larger than our revenue a year ago in the same quarter. Think about that. Same company, same people, extenuated products... This is all the result of being right about product, right about execution, and standing in the headwinds of people who are certain they're right."

— Alex Karp, Chief Executive Officer

"When you want AI to work in production in a real enterprise at real scale where there is no room for slop, there is only one platform: AIP. It is not just the playbook of cutting costs... AIP is the battle-tested platform that allows the wholesale redefinition of how companies compete."

— Ryan Taylor, Chief Revenue Officer and Chief Legal Officer

For over two years now, we have been saying that while LLMs are improving, models are converging and the cost per token continues to drop precipitously. GPT-4 equivalent performance that cost $20 per million tokens in early 2023 is now approximately a thousand times cheaper three years later. Because of this increased efficiency, use case demand for tokens is exploding. Our AIP workflows today utilize vastly more tokens. This includes agents orchestrating across the ontology, chaining reasoning, tool use, retrieval, and execution. And it's growing. This is Jevons' Paradox. It's the single most important dynamic in enterprise software right now. When the Victorians built more efficient steam engines, everyone assumed coal consumption would fall. Instead, it skyrocketed. Cheaper transport meant more demand for transport. Tokens are the new coal; AIP is the train. As inference gets cheaper, the number of tasks that you can economically assign to AI grows exponentially. Precisely because tokens are so much cheaper, agents can in principle benefit by consuming so many more tokens to reason, plan, and execute multi-step workflows. But in practice, the number of tasks that you can trust a model with without the right harness exponentially declines. More tokens means more slop. And the more commodity cognition you consume, the more you need a system that can prevent the economic harm so you can harness the economic value. That system is AIP. That intermediary representation is the ontology. This is also why we are seeing the death of legacy software. AIP replaces static workflows not by replicating the playbook, but by eliminating the need for one. At Thomas Cavanagh Construction, 97% of their employees use Foundry every day. Every other piece of software must now justify its existence, and so far, they haven't been able to. We're seeing this internally too. This quarter, we replaced our old expensive CRM with an AI-first solution built on AIP in a few months that users absolutely love. Our customers are seeing the real value is not automating what you already do; it's doing what was previously impossible. A major Telco set out to automate 10 million customer calls a year. The real insight was that the most dissatisfied customers never call; they churn silently. The reframe was counterintuitive. Don't use AI to reduce calls; use it to generate them. An AI advocate that proactively calls on every customer's behalf. The point is simple: use AI to do more work, work that was never economically feasible before AIP. For every agent action, our customers need to answer three questions: Who authorized this? What did it cost? Can I trust what it did? These questions need exact answers with precision. There's no tolerance for slop. We're building a platform-native Agent Engine SDK, a single set of primitives we're building, persisting, governing, and operating ontology-native agents. This is a common layer that lets you visualize every agent in your enterprise and control it, regardless of how it was built. A true Agent Operating System. On top of that, we provide unified cost attribution per agent, per session, and per workflow, with administrative caps. We offer full provenance so every ontology mutation traces back to the agent and reasoning chain that produced it. Security marking propagation flows from input data through agent sessions onto all output, with approval gates for any workflow that could reclassify information. That's how you get a CISO, a CFO, and a combatant commander to say yes. AIP is the no-slop zone, the platform where every agent action is governed, attributed, and auditable. Turning to the US government, on the foxhole side, Maven met its moment across real-world events in Q1. Usage has doubled in the past four months through the end of March and is now 4x over the past 12 months across the services, the combatant commands, the Joint Staff, and the intelligence community. When the stakes are highest, when failure is measured in lives and readiness, this is where we are uniquely positioned. On the factory floor side, the demand on the defense industrial base to ramp production and sustainment has been so acute that we have surged resources from our commercial business. This is exactly what Warp Speed was built for: modernized American manufacturing. And we're doing just that where it counts the most. AIP is the default builder platform in the Department of War, with thousands of developers using AIFD, migrating legacy systems, standing up new capabilities, and solving problems that used to require contractor teams and months of lead time. Our software is becoming the most malleable and responsive weapon system for the Joint Force. Finally, what's now clear is that Mythos and Spud, and even other current generation models with AIP, are capable of finding novel vulnerabilities in complex cyber kill chains. They have discovered thousands of zero-days in major operating systems and browsers. This is the Spud-Nik moment in the AI arms race. The rate of vulnerability identification is about to skyrocket. Finding the bugs is no longer the limiting factor. Rapid-fire remediation with exact precision, immediacy, and absolute certainty is the new hard problem. Knowing exactly what versions of what software are running where and closing the remediation chain autonomously is vital. Apollo was built for exactly this. We're shipping the next generation of Apollo as we help our customers reposter for this world. Note the Jevons' Paradox dynamic here too: more AI means more code, more code means more slop, more slop means more attack surface, more attack surface means more vulnerabilities, and more vulnerabilities means more Apollo. You can't lump what we're doing in with others. We're really providing infrastructure and the installation of AI infrastructure. If your company is largely running around and offering steak dinners with something that someone can hack and rebuild in a week, yes, you're going to have a huge problem in this market, and those companies are going to have a hard time. That's life, like all sorts of movements that don't make sense. They're under huge pressure. And that's one of the reasons we're at the forefront. I mean, can you believe we're at the forefront of almost every discussion in the world? It is simply because we're powering almost everything that works. Not everything, there's some other great companies out there, many of them are not well known and we should help publicize them, but we're at the front, and that's what these numbers show. You don't have to believe us, believe your non-lying eyes. Thank you, Alex. As always, we have a lot of individual investors on the line. Is there anything you'd like to say before we end the call? Well, to individual investors and Palantirians who are also individual investors, being on the front line of important things is painful. You get yelled at occasionally, and many of the people yelling at you have no clue what they're saying. Some of the people do have a clue what they're saying and just disagree with the West being strong and more efficient and more moral and having better unit economics. Or quite frankly, they are stuck in the illusion of AI slop. We value your support and we value your defense of us. We are defending you every day, every day, and that's in great part what drives these results. And we are having some fun doing it too, just so you know, and hopefully you'll have some fun. Thank you for your support and we will see you next quarter. Thank you, that concludes Q&A for today's call.

WATCH: Vice President JD Vance delivers remarks at Iowa campaign event

Fox News(15.3M) ·36:02 ·33.5K views · 2026-05-05
JD Vance (Vice President) Zach Nunn (US Representative, Iowa)
Vice President JD Vance framed the upcoming 2026 elections as a fundamental choice between a government that prioritizes American citizens and workers through "common sense" economic protectionism and anti-fraud measures, or one that favors special interests and illegal immigrants.
TL;DR Vice President JD Vance framed the upcoming 2026 elections as a fundamental choice between a government that prioritizes American citizens and workers through "common sense" economic protectionism and anti-fraud measures, or one that favors special interests and illegal...

TL;DR

Vice President JD Vance framed the upcoming 2026 elections as a fundamental choice between a government that prioritizes American citizens and workers through "common sense" economic protectionism and anti-fraud measures, or one that favors special interests and illegal immigrants. Rallying for Representative Zach Nunn, Vance highlighted the administration's focus on Iowa agriculture, domestic manufacturing, and fiscal accountability.

Economic Protectionism and Manufacturing

  • Support for Domestic Industry: Vance shared a narrative of an Iowa factory nearly driven out of business by Chinese "dumping" and slave labor, contrasting this with the administration’s current trade stance.
      • Tariff Policy: Stressed that foreign countries attempting to undercut Iowa workers must pay a "big fat tariff" to protect domestic jobs.
      • Tax Incentives: Credited the Working Families Tax Cuts, supported by Rep. Zach Nunn, for allowing businesses to increase bonuses, salaries, and staffing.
  • Housing and Foreign Investment: Linked the rising cost of living to foreign and corporate ownership of American assets.
      • Prioritizing Families: Argued that American homes should belong to families rather than foreign investors or Chinese entities buying farmland.
      • Immigration Link: Suggested that housing costs are exacerbated by the presence of millions of illegal immigrants and called for border security as a primary tool for lowering rent.

Federal Oversight and the Fraud Task Force

  • Eradicating Government Waste: As leader of the federal fraud task force, Vance emphasized that taxpayer dollars must be protected from systemic abuse.
      • SNAP Benefits Abuse: Reported that Agriculture Secretary Brooke Rollins identified 186,000 deceased individuals and 355,000 people receiving double benefits under the SNAP program.
      • Subpoena Power: Confirmed that the task force served 22 investigatory subpoenas to the Department of Justice in just three months to prosecute fraudsters.
  • Targeting Welfare Fraud: Highlighted a specific case in Minneapolis where funds intended for parents of children with autism were allegedly diverted to "Somalian fraudsters" through identity fraud.
      • Federal Audits: Noted that the administration is threatening to cut off federal funding to states that refuse to audit benefit recipients to confirm eligibility.

Agriculture and Trade Expansion

  • Market Access: Claimed the administration has doubled the export market for Iowa farmers in the last 18 months by using trade authorities to force foreign countries to accept U.S. agricultural products.
  • Biofuels and Energy:
      • E15 Support: Voiced strong support for Rep. Zach Nunn’s legislation to expand the sale of E15 fuel nationwide to benefit Iowa corn growers.
      • Input Costs: Acknowledged the struggle with high fertilizer prices and committed to finding ways to lower these costs for the farming community.

Political Contrast and Campaign Strategy

  • Demographic Shift: Vance, citing his own upbringing in a "union Democrat" family, argued that the modern Democratic Party has abandoned working people in favor of social issues.
  • Legislative Critique: Attacked opponent Sarah Trone Garret’s voting record, specifically regarding gender transition surgeries for minors and biological males in women's sports.
  • The "Common Sense" Mandate: Defined the Republican platform as a return to simple principles: "American government ought to be fighting for America's citizens rather than illegal aliens."
  • Honoring Sacrifice: Closed with a reflection on meeting Gold Star families in Des Moines, arguing that responsible governance is a way to "earn" the ultimate sacrifice made by members of the military.
"Finding fraud in the federal government, it's kind of like fishing in a barrel with dynamite... I am shocked every single day by the things that we find." — JD Vance
"We have two parties in Washington DC... it's a heartbreaking thing for a kid who came from a union Democrat family to realize that Democrats these days, they seem to care more about gender transition than they do about you keeping more of your hard-earned money." — JD Vance
"Part of how we earn that incredible sacrifice given to all of us is by making this country's politics and government worthy of the people who put on the uniform and will never see their loved ones again." — JD Vance

And so I get in the car with my little six-year-old, and I look into those big eyes—his eyes remind me of his mother's eyes—and I think to myself, "What an amazing blessing it is to be a father in the freest and most prosperous country anywhere in the history of the world." I thought to myself: what would I say if this beautiful six-year-old boy got older and decided, like his dad, to put on the uniform of his country? And I thought to myself, on the one hand, I'd be so proud of him, but on the other hand, I'd be so terrified that what happened to those two families would happen to this boy. It hit me that every time we lose somebody, every time somebody goes overseas and sacrifices their life, every time that a person gives the ultimate sacrifice to the United States of America, we often read about it as a line in a newspaper or online. But there's a father, a mother, a grandma, aunts, uncles, and a whole crew of people who love them the same way that we all love every single member of our family. You take that love and you set that on one side, and you consider the balance that all of us owe. Because on the other side, we have to meet their sacrifice by carrying something forward that they can't carry forward. We have to make this country worthy of that sacrifice. You remember that movie *Saving Private Ryan*? It's one of my favorite movies. At the very end, right before one of the soldiers takes his last breath, he looks up and he says, "Earn this." And what he means is, all that love, all that was taken away from those families, all that was taken away from so many of the people who have put on the uniform and sacrificed for this country—we have to earn it. Now, so much of that is how you live your life. So much of that is Congressman Zach Nunn being a good husband and father in his beautiful family here. I think what you guys have, six or seven? Six. She is a saint, Zach, she is a saint. Part of that is how we go to work and treat our employees and what we build and make with our hands and with our minds. Part of it is how we go to church and give back to our community. But part of how we earn that incredible sacrifice given to all of us is by making this country's politics and government worthy of the people who put on the uniform and will never see their loved ones again. Part of what we have to do, my friends, is every single day we have to send people to Washington. I'm not saying you have to agree with every single issue. I'm saying that you gotta send people to Washington who wake up every single day and recognize that they fight for you. That's how we honor this sacrifice, that's how we make this country great again, and that's how we make 250 years of American history and American patriots proud. God bless you guys and thank you for having me in Iowa.

LIVE: Hegseth And Caine Hold Pentagon Press Briefing On The Iran War

Forbes Breaking News(5.5M) ·39:06 ·15.4K views · 2026-05-05
Pete Hegseth (Secretary of War) Dan Caine (Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff)
The Department of Defense has launched "Project Freedom," a defensive maritime operation led by U.S.
TL;DR The Department of Defense has launched "Project Freedom," a defensive maritime operation led by U.S. Central Command (CENTCOM) to secure the Strait of Hormuz, break Iran’s illegal blockade, and restore the free flow of global commerce. While a ceasefire remains in place,...

TL;DR

The Department of Defense has launched "Project Freedom," a defensive maritime operation led by U.S. Central Command (CENTCOM) to secure the Strait of Hormuz, break Iran’s illegal blockade, and restore the free flow of global commerce. While a ceasefire remains in place, the U.S. has established a "red, white, and blue dome" of protection over the waterway and warned Iran that any aggression will be met with overwhelming firepower.

Project Freedom: Scope and Objectives

  • Mission Profile: Secretary Pete Hegseth defined the operation as defensive in nature, focused in scope, and temporary in duration. It is distinct from the previous "Operation Epic Fury."
  • Primary Goal: To protect innocent commercial shipping from Iranian "extortion," including illegal tolling systems and harassment of civilian tankers.
  • Current Status: Two U.S. commercial ships and accompanying destroyers have already successfully transited the strait. Currently, 22,500 mariners and over 1,550 commercial vessels remain trapped in the Arabian Gulf awaiting safe passage.
  • Blockade Enforcement: While opening the strait for international commerce, the U.S. "ironclad blockade" against Iranian ports remains in full effect; six Iranian ships attempting to run the blockade were recently turned back.

Tactical Assets and Defensive Capabilities

  • "The Dome" of Protection: General Dan Caine reported that an enhanced security area has been established on the southern side of the strait, protected by a synchronized layer of land, naval, and air assets.
  • Force Composition:
      • Personnel: Over 15,000 American service members are currently dedicated to the mission.
      • Aviation: More than 100 fighters, attack aircraft, and drones provide 24/7 overwatch.
      • Command & Control: The 82nd Airborne Division is coordinating All-Domain Command and Control (JADC2) using AI-enabled tactical networks to synchronize effects across sea, air, and cyber domains.
  • Recent Engagements: Since the ceasefire was announced, Iran has attacked commercial vessels nine times and U.S. forces over ten times. U.S. Navy MH-60 and Army AH-64 Apache helicopters recently defeated Iranian cruise missiles, drones, and small boats targeting the strait.

Strategic Posture and Diplomacy

  • Ceasefire Status: Secretary Hegseth clarified that the ceasefire is not over, but described the U.S. military as "locked and loaded" to resume major combat operations if Iran escalates.
  • Nuclear Ambitions: The administration maintains that "Operation Midnight Hammer" successfully dismantled Iranian conventional capabilities and set back their nuclear program. Hegseth reiterated that the ultimate goal is a deal ensuring Iran never acquires a nuclear weapon.
  • Exit Strategy: The U.S. intends to hand over responsibility for the waterway to international partners. Hegseth noted that the "world needs this waterway a lot more than we do" and called on nations like South Korea, Japan, and Australia to assist in defending their own commercial interests.

Regional Threats and Allied Coordination

  • Iranian Aggression: Beyond the strait, Iran has recently targeted Oman once and the UAE three times, including an unsuccessful attack on the Fujairah oil terminal.
  • U.S.-Israel Alignment: Responding to questions about Israeli intent to collapse the Iranian government, Hegseth emphasized that while Israel is a capable partner, President Trump is "the only one hand on the wheel" directing U.S. strategy based on "America First" interests.
  • War Powers: Following the February 28 termination of formal hostilities, the administration views the 60-day War Powers clock as stopped, though the President retains the authority to restart operations if the ceasefire is breached.
